<span id="freeTextContainer1750715423152351639">When Theo agrees to print a traveling showman's pamphlet, he only thinks of the money it will bring in. Instead, it sets off a chain reaction that results in the smashing of the press and the murder of his master. Caught on the wrong side of the law, Theo must flee the city. Soon, he has teamed up with the traveling showman Count Las Bombas (who is actually a con artist) a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1750715423152351639">When Theo agrees to print a traveling showman's pamphlet, he only thinks of the money it will bring in. Instead, it sets off a chain reaction that results in the smashing of the press and the murder of his master. Caught on the wrong side of the law, Theo must flee the city. Soon, he has teamed up with the traveling showman Count Las Bombas (who is actually a con artist) and his servant. The trio is soon joined by Mickle, a clever, strong-willed girl with a mysterious past. Performing feats that astound and amaze, the motley crew falls into a trap set by Chief Minister Cabbarus, who is determined to wrest power from the grief-stricken king. Now they must not only save themselves-they must save the kingdom...</span>

        <a href="/review/show/67424423?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 14, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/50378-angie" class="user" title="Angie">Angie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=belovedbookshelf" class="actionLinkLite">belovedbookshelf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer67424423">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8995080063831812455"><a title="Lloyd Alexander" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8924.Lloyd_Alexander">Lloyd Alexander</a> is one of a handful of authors who had a hand in forming who I am today. At the beginning of sixth grade my teacher pulled out <a title="The Return of the King (The Lord of the Rings, Part 3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18512.The_Return_of_the_King__The_Lord_of_the_Rings__Part_3_">The Book of Three</a>, the first in Alexander's Chronicles of Prydain, and began reading. He did all the voices, from opinionated Eilonwy to noble Gwydion to humble Gurgi with his poor, tender head. We sat there enchanted as he read the entire five-book series aloud to the class. We were living overseas at the time and, unfortunately, we had limited access to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8995080063831812455"><a title="Lloyd Alexander" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8924.Lloyd_Alexander">Lloyd Alexander</a> is one of a handful of authors who had a hand in forming who I am today. At the beginning of sixth grade my teacher pulled out <a title="The Return of the King (The Lord of the Rings, Part 3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18512.The_Return_of_the_King__The_Lord_of_the_Rings__Part_3_">The Book of Three</a>, the first in Alexander's Chronicles of Prydain, and began reading. He did all the voices, from opinionated Eilonwy to noble Gwydion to humble Gurgi with his poor, tender head. We sat there enchanted as he read the entire five-book series aloud to the class. We were living overseas at the time and, unfortunately, we had limited access to books. When we moved back to the states, we stopped in at the local library and I immediately went to the A section to see if they had any other Alexander books. I was in luck. I picked up WESTMARK first because of the cover and because I read the first line and was completely sold.<br /><br />"Theo, by occupation, was a devil."<br /><br />When the librarian informed me it was the first in a trilogy, I quickly grabbed the other two and made for the door. They were utterly different from the Chronicles of Prydain--darker, and not really fantasy at all, though they are set in a fictional kingdom. Alexander is so well-known for the Chronicles of Prydain and it seems to me this little gem of a trilogy hasn't gotten quite the same reception, though WESTMARK actually won the National Book Award in 1982. I have re-read them many times since the first time and I love them more with every encounter.<br /><br />Main character Theo is, in fact, a devil. Though not the kind you might be expecting. Theo is a printer's devil--an apprentice to the printer Anton in the small town of Dorning in the kingdom of Westmark. After printing a pamphlet by Dr. Absalom, Theo and his master are forced to flee into the night as guards break into the printing press and burn the shop to the ground. Ever since Chief Minister Cabbarus took over the running of the kingdom from their grieving king, he has been systematically curtailing the freedoms of the people. On the run from the law, Theo finds himself in league with the mysterious Dr. Absalom, also known as Count Las Bombas, the trusty dwarf Musket, and the bright but haunted girl Mickle--a former pickpocket and street urchin. But when the demands of his conscience prove to much to bear, Theo strikes out on his own and takes a job as scribe for a small group of revolutionaries led by the charismatic Florian. As the story builds to its heart-palpitating climax, these two bands find themselves inexplicably drawn to the capitol city of Marianstat and into the grasping hands of the sinister Cabbarus.<br /><br />I love how perfectly paced <a title="Lloyd Alexander" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8924.Lloyd_Alexander">Lloyd Alexander</a>'s writing always is. He truly was a master at constructing the ebb and flow necessary to a genuinely riveting storyline, the heights and depths in which to lead his characters, and the clever and crafty words to put in their mouths. His main characters are so far from perfect and they are often painfully aware of it. They want so badly to do the right thing and yet they are constantly faced with how difficult and conflicting a desire that is. Theo is no exception. He is a simple young man hurled into a complex web of secrets and plotting not of his making. The world and conflict is based on the French Revolution and the pain and ambiguity of that conflict is not spared in Alexander's fictional version, particularly in the sequel, <a title="The Stinky Cheese Man and Other Fairly Stupid Tales by Jon Scieszka" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/407429.The_Stinky_Cheese_Man_and_Other_Fairly_Stupid_Tales">The Kestrel</a>, where Theo and his companions are caught up in bloody battle as the nation tears itself apart in the name of freedom. But that trademark humor and overwhelming compassion are still there. It's a beautiful series filled with a host of fine characters (some delightful, some dreadful) who spend their lives wrestling with questions of morality, purpose, and honor, and leavened by roguish wit, high adventure, and a sweet romance. Highly recommended for fans of <a title="Megan Whalen Turner" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner">Megan Whalen Turner</a>'s Queen's Thief series.<br /><br />Reading order: WESTMARK, <a title="The Stinky Cheese Man and Other Fairly Stupid Tales by Jon Scieszka" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/407429.The_Stinky_Cheese_Man_and_Other_Fairly_Stupid_Tales">The Kestrel</a>, <a title="The Beggar Queen (Firebird) by Lloyd Alexander" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/116435.The_Beggar_Queen__Firebird_">The Beggar Queen</a>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8995080063831812455">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/652877-flannery" class="user" title="Flannery">Flannery</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Flannery by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/50378-angie">Angie</a>
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=young-adult-teen" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult-teen</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=swords-and-lasers" class="actionLinkLite">swords-and-lasers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=kcls" class="actionLinkLite">kcls</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer422576154">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8500152588750545021"><em>Westmark</em> is a compact, quick-paced start to a fantasy series and it is the first of Alexander's works I've read. It won't be the last, as I already intend to finish this series sooner rather than later. Theo, the main character, is apprentice to a printer in a kingdom where the king rules in name only, as he's been overcome with grief since the disappearance of his daughter years before. In his stead, Chief Minister Cabbarus rules with an iron fist and ridiculous ineptitude. When Theo agrees to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8500152588750545021"><em>Westmark</em> is a compact, quick-paced start to a fantasy series and it is the first of Alexander's works I've read. It won't be the last, as I already intend to finish this series sooner rather than later. Theo, the main character, is apprentice to a printer in a kingdom where the king rules in name only, as he's been overcome with grief since the disappearance of his daughter years before. In his stead, Chief Minister Cabbarus rules with an iron fist and ridiculous ineptitude. When Theo agrees to print up an order for Musket, a dwarf working for a traveling magician/con man Dr. Absalom, it runs contrary to the Cabbarus' rules and sets up a story of escape, evasion, and intrigue. Theo becomes part of Absalom's show, along with Musket and Mickle, a young street urchin girl. Though the outcome is predictable, I was pleasantly surprised by the road the characters took to get there and by several plot twists. If you're looking for an entry point into Lloyd Alexander's fantasy books, this one is perfect. At least, it was for me. On to the next!<br /><br />This mini-review was part of a series of 7 mini-reviews of short YA books I wrote for a post over at our blog, <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/10/7-mini-reviews-of-short-ya-books-some-whackadoo-story-ideas.html">The Readventurer</a>.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/45868891?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 25, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/124819-wendy" class="user" title="Wendy">Wendy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/124819-wendy?shelf=sf-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">sf-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer45868891">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16936026382847423173">A smart, fast-paced YA fantasy. Two things really impress me about this book. First, the sheer economy of language with which Alexander makes a large cast of characters vivid and keeps the plot moving. This book accomplishes more in ~185 pages than many a doorstopper fantasy accomplishes in twice the space. (Which is good, because once I started it, I didn't really want to put it down.)<br /><br />Second, Alexander does a great job of making his characters have different goals and points of view. Being a go</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16936026382847423173">A smart, fast-paced YA fantasy. Two things really impress me about this book. First, the sheer economy of language with which Alexander makes a large cast of characters vivid and keeps the plot moving. This book accomplishes more in ~185 pages than many a doorstopper fantasy accomplishes in twice the space. (Which is good, because once I started it, I didn't really want to put it down.)<br /><br />Second, Alexander does a great job of making his characters have different goals and points of view. Being a good guy in this book is a complicated thing - it doesn't mean that you want the same thing as all the other good guys. <br /><br />Finally, anyone who's ever criticized fantasy for being generally politically retrograde will be pleased to hear that while some characters are out to restore the rightful monarch to the throne, some are much more interested in seeing the people of Westmark rule. (Personally, I've been wishing for ages for more fantasy novels in which the characters fight to restore the just and rightful democracy, and Lloyd Alexander's had one for a couple of decades now.)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16936026382847423173">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer7410632855043179832">Here's a HUGE coincidence. I remember reading this book/series in 5th grade and I LOVED IT! I checked this book out over and over and just was enthralled with it. For YEARS now, YEARS mind you, I was trying to remember the name of this book. I googled everything I could possibly remember about this book to no avail. THEN, a couple of days ago, I was in a thrift store and I literally found MY BOOK! The cover I remembered, it had been purchased from the library where I had checked it out and there</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7410632855043179832">Here's a HUGE coincidence. I remember reading this book/series in 5th grade and I LOVED IT! I checked this book out over and over and just was enthralled with it. For YEARS now, YEARS mind you, I was trying to remember the name of this book. I googled everything I could possibly remember about this book to no avail. THEN, a couple of days ago, I was in a thrift store and I literally found MY BOOK! The cover I remembered, it had been purchased from the library where I had checked it out and there it WAS!!! For 50 cents!! So happy to be reunited! I'm rereading and is EXCEPTIONALLY more exciting now that I have an adult perspective and can understand plot &amp; have a better appreciation for characters and development. AWESOME BOOK!! :) HOORAY FOR SERENDIPITY!!! :)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_231721976">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231721976" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6879652-mara" class="left imgcol" title="Mara"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1380254226p2/6879652.jpg" alt="Mara" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/231721976?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 21, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6879652-mara" class="user" title="Mara">Mara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1586058.Westmark" title="Hardcover 9780525423355" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6879652-mara?shelf=books-owned" class="actionLinkLite">books-owned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6879652-mara?shelf=adventure" class="actionLinkLite">adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6879652-mara?shelf=4-stars" class="actionLinkLite">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer231721976">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17620187146538215656"><strong>Cover Blurb:</strong> Yes or No? Divided; it initially caught my interest many years back because it looked like an awesome historical adventure story, but I personally am not a fan of the artwork. It’s too . . . harsh.<br /><br /><strong>Characters:</strong> Lloyd Alexander is wonderful at creating memorable characters, and I personally think that his most memorable cast is in this trilogy. I am not a fan of Theo name, the protagonist, but I love Theo himself. He’s the right age to have an adventure and he’s honest. Las Bombas remi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17620187146538215656"><strong>Cover Blurb:</strong> Yes or No? Divided; it initially caught my interest many years back because it looked like an awesome historical adventure story, but I personally am not a fan of the artwork. It’s too . . . harsh.<br /><br /><strong>Characters:</strong> Lloyd Alexander is wonderful at creating memorable characters, and I personally think that his most memorable cast is in this trilogy. I am not a fan of Theo name, the protagonist, but I love Theo himself. He’s the right age to have an adventure and he’s honest. Las Bombas reminds me of Mr. Tigg from <em>Martin Chuzzlewit</em> - a conman, not wholly a bad man (Mr. Tigg is a scoundrel, but he cared for Bailey), and bursting with personality. Musket, the dwarf, for some reason really struck a chord with me. He doesn’t really have all that much dialogue in the book, but he’s a spunky and memorable character. If Westmark were ever turned into a movie, Warwick Davis would be perfect for Musket. Cabbarus is an acceptable villain, but he isn’t the most impressive I’ve met. He’s a little too full of himself, which causes him to make mistakes, but he is also cold-hearted enough that I wouldn’t want to meet him. And then Mickle . . . I love Mickle. She’s clever, practical, and sarcastic without having The Attitude.<br /><br /><strong>The Romance:</strong> It is hardly mentioned in the story. Theo and Mickle like each other, but the Author doesn’t let their attraction get in the way of what is, at its heart, a good adventure story. It is the sort of romance a story like this needs: clearly there, but not overbearing, doesn’t make the characters start behaving ridiculously, and really doesn’t even come up as an issue until the very end.<br /><br /><strong>Plot:</strong> As I have said, it’s an adventure story, and it has all the elements that are needed. A protagonist turned fugitive by no fault of his own, a flamboyant personality the protagonist later meets up with (in this case, Las Bombas), street urchins, a group of revolutionaries, a jail break, and of course the villain’s downfall. I love the era the Author chose for his story - 1700s - and I really liked the twist in the end. It’s a twist that has been done countless times, but the Author pulls it off because he doesn’t make it at all obvious until it is actually revealed. <br /><br /><strong>Believability:</strong> Cabbarus’s plans for taking over the throne are entirely plausible. It is a plan that could very easily go wrong, true, but that’s the beauty of fiction: in a book, that evil plan doesn’t have to go wrong, so long as there is a possibility that it could work.<br /><br /><strong>Writing Style:</strong> I do like Lloyd Alexander’s style. He has great wit, and it is a simple, pleasing style that suits adventure stories very well. He knows how to bring his characters to life with very few words, but in those few words, he conveys so much about them. <em>Westmark</em> is no exception.<br /><br /><strong>Content:</strong> None.<br /><br /><strong>Conclusion:</strong> The one major flaw I have always found in Alexander’s stories are his endings. I have always found them to be very weak. It’s like he writes and writes, and then gets bored with the story and just cobbles together an ending that either is so bizarre that it leaves you with a question mark hovering above your head, or it’s just bloody abrupt. The conclusion to <em>Westmark</em> is bloody abrupt, but what saves it is the fact that the book has a sequel, so an abrupt ending is acceptable in this case. I read this book a long time ago, and loved it as a kid. Re-reading it now that I’m older, I still love it. There’s just nothing not to like. The characters, the story, the world itself - it’s all wonderful.<br /><br /><strong>Recommended Audience:</strong> Girl-and-guy read, any age. Readers of “swashbucklers” would love this. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17620187146538215656">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_250244980">

  <a href="/user/show/3450884-barbara" class="left imgcol" title="Barbara"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Barbara" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/250244980?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 22, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3450884-barbara" class="user" title="Barbara">Barbara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3450884-barbara?shelf=action-adventure" class="actionLinkLite">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3450884-barbara?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer250244980">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17030841282405289113">The first time I read this novel, I really couldn't get into it that much and considered it inferior to the author's other series, The Prydain Chronicles. I was wrong; this trilogy stands among the very best of young adult literature and I wish it were included in the reading lists of English classes. <br /><br />Westmark is a country where the king has lost his will to live due to the believed premature death of his daughter, Augusta, and Carabbus (the chief minister) has surreptitiously taken over. My fir</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17030841282405289113">The first time I read this novel, I really couldn't get into it that much and considered it inferior to the author's other series, The Prydain Chronicles. I was wrong; this trilogy stands among the very best of young adult literature and I wish it were included in the reading lists of English classes. <br /><br />Westmark is a country where the king has lost his will to live due to the believed premature death of his daughter, Augusta, and Carabbus (the chief minister) has surreptitiously taken over. My firs thought was that this sounds a bit like "The Two Towers" where Grima Wormtongue speaks for the possessed King Theoden. Carabbus has instituted a reign of terror and there is great discontent amongst the military, peasantry, and nobility of the realm. <br /><br />Entering into this volatile mix is Theo, a printer's devil (assistant) who witnesses the cold-blooded murder of his master at the hands of Royal Guards and questions his pacifist stance after falling in with Count Las Bombas, a rogue; Musket, a warriorlike dwarf, and the mysterious Mickle, a street urchin. <br /><br />The book is a young adult primer on the psychology of war and its justification; violence is seen through the eyes of those who inflict it and those who suffer from it. The writing is sparse and much of the detail found in The Prydain Chronicles is gone, however, that does not diminish the book's characterizations. <br /><br />I highly recommend this book and its two sequels, The Kestrel and The Beggar Queen.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_379466604">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379466604" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/163451-julianne" class="left imgcol" title="Julianne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1200811733p2/163451.jpg" alt="Julianne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/379466604?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/163451-julianne" class="user" title="Julianne">Julianne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/883423.Westmark" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440997313" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/163451-julianne?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer379466604">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2532973102887199737">Like most readers, I first encountered and read this book many years ago. So long ago, in fact, that I could not finish it in a day. I remember taking it with me on a visit to my grandparents' summer cottage and staying up to all hours of the night in order to reach the mind-bending (at the time) conclusion. It was probably about 2:00 in the morning by the time Theo &amp; Co. found themselves being forced into charlatanry by their own government (Oh, the irony!), and I remember being incredibly</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2532973102887199737">Like most readers, I first encountered and read this book many years ago. So long ago, in fact, that I could not finish it in a day. I remember taking it with me on a visit to my grandparents' summer cottage and staying up to all hours of the night in order to reach the mind-bending (at the time) conclusion. It was probably about 2:00 in the morning by the time Theo &amp; Co. found themselves being forced into charlatanry by their own government (Oh, the irony!), and I remember being incredibly creeped out by the yawning well shaft and the revelations that followed. The kind of creeped out that makes your hair stand up, your flesh crawl, and your blood run cold.<br /><br />I've re-read the book two or three times since, and while the ending no longer creeps me out, the story still enthralls me. Theo, a former printer's devil and "lover of virtue," is the kind of hero I can get behind. One who notices what others don't, who ponders, who wonders and asks questions. He's certainly not incapable of taking action. However, the actions he takes are often (as with us) in response to circumstances beyond his control, and as such, are products of the moment, not completely intentional, and less appropriate, less heroic than Theo would like. Whenever Theo takes action, he seems to feel a little worse about himself than he did before. One gets the sense he is trying to live up to an unrealizable ideal, one he is as incapable of modifying as he is of embodying.<br /><br />On the other end of the spectrum, Cabbarus is the kind of villain I can get behind. Cold and calculating, but not consciously or intentionally evil. In fact, Cabbarus is defined by nothing so much as his single-minded devotion to his own ideals of justice and virtue. Unlike so many fictional villains, he does not immediately create an impression of evil in the minds of his beholders. Rather, his glance "made all on whom it rested feel, in comparison with him, less noble, less high-minded, and that their linen needed changing" (35). In a certain sense, Cabbarus embodies, in the eyes of many, the sort of ideal that Theo carries in his mind. One could say that the chief difference between the two characters is Cabbarus's tendency to self-satisfaction, compared to Theo's self-dissatisfaction. Cabbarus tends to blame others when his schemes fail to produce his intended results; Theo tends to blame himself.<br /><br />Thankfully, in addition to these two very different lovers of virtue, Westmark abounds in characters who don't really give a flying fig about all that. Characters who care more about the amount of food in their bellies (which after all, is very different from the amount of money in their purses) than about living up to anyone's ideal. This would include Theo's companions Count Las Bombas (aka Dr. Absalom, aka Mynheer Bloomsa, aka "whatever he's calling himself at the moment" (p. 110)), Musket, Mickle, and the two water rats Sparrow and Weasel. It is no accident that these characters all occupy some of the lowest rungs of society. Las Bombas and Musket (himself rescued from "the beggar factory") drift from town to town, rootless, residence-less--unless one counts their roomy coach as a residence. They are, in modern parlance, "homeless." Mickle, when we first encounter her, is a guttersnipe, a "collection of skin and bones" (p. 53), former apprentice to a thief who was hanged, illiterate as a bird (though not by choice). On perhaps the very lowest rung are Sparrow and Weasel, orphaned sister and brother, who survive by scavenging, an activity that extends to picking dead men's pockets. Their views on morality may be best summed up in this exchange with Keller, writer of a satirical journal:<br /><br />"Water rats, I shall ask you a question. Are you thieves?"<br /><br />"No," piped up Weasel, "but I'd like to be."<br /><br />"I'm no thief either," said Sparrow. "I never had the luck." (p. 106)<br /><br />In this world of the dispossessed and protector-less, practicality rather than morality is paramount. The concern is not with the world or the self as it should be, but as it is, and whatever actions are best calculated to enhance one's own survival (and the survival of those one cares about) are the "right" things to do. It is appropriate that Sparrow, much later, turns "out to be a demon at arithmetic" (<em>The Beggar Queen</em>, p. 24). Sparrow has been forced to become a quick and accurate calculator by living in a world of scarcity--or maybe she was born with the ability to grasp arithmetical concepts intuitively and that is why she and Weasel survive.<br /><br />This is not to say that Alexander is saying virtue is a luxury for the rich or even for the reasonably well-fed. Rather, he seems to be pointing out that one's conception of virtue has a lot to do with one's own perspective and that this perspective is shaped to a great extent by one's circumstances. Many of the novel's "good" characters (a distinction that becomes increasingly meaningless the longer one reads in the series) grasp this concept out of hand. It is Cabbarus's great failing that he does not. It is Theo's great good luck that he finds himself plunged in circumstances that call his own ideals into question...and to his great good credit that he chooses to live through the questions. That he has managed to do so is attested in the last few pages by his admission to Las Bombas, "I'm not the one to blame you either. I was trying to be better than I am. I'm not as virtuous as I thought I was--or wanted to be. I wonder if anyone is, even Florian. I suppose we should be glad if we're able to do any good at all" (p. 183). It is appropriate that Theo finds such satisfaction in Florian's note to him, delivered 2 pages later, "My Child, You did well. Perhaps you even did right." When I first read the book, I thought Theo smiled at Florian's finally calling him "My Child." Now, I think Theo smiles because even Florian acknowledges he isn't absolutely certain what is right and what is wrong. Perhaps Theo recognizes that this simple fact binds the two of them together in a way Florian's good opinion of him could never do.<br /><br />On the copyright page of my edition, Alexander notes this book is "For those who regret their many imperfections, but know it would be worse having none at all." A telling dedication, indeed. Appropriate for all readers, certainly, but perhaps especially appropriate for the young adults who are ostensibly this book's intended audience.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2532973102887199737">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1130284067">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130284067" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/33911745-aelvana" class="left imgcol" title="Aelvana"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Aelvana" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1130284067?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 12, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/33911745-aelvana" class="user" title="Aelvana">Aelvana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1130284067">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4284035267772618308">Theo thought to help his master by taking on a job to print some pamphlets, but his actions inadvertently lead to his master's murder and himself becoming a fugitive. On the road, he joins a rouge, a dwarf, and a street girl in their con schemes. Theo isn't comfortable with the deception, or with his own actions the night his master was murdered. In the larger world, the Chief Minister Cabberus schemes for the throne of Westmark, forcing increasingly draconian policies on the country. That intri</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4284035267772618308">Theo thought to help his master by taking on a job to print some pamphlets, but his actions inadvertently lead to his master's murder and himself becoming a fugitive. On the road, he joins a rouge, a dwarf, and a street girl in their con schemes. Theo isn't comfortable with the deception, or with his own actions the night his master was murdered. In the larger world, the Chief Minister Cabberus schemes for the throne of Westmark, forcing increasingly draconian policies on the country. That intrigue works its way down even to Theo, whose actions may save the country. . . or destroy it.<br /><br />Westmark is in many ways a simple story, told in spare prose that is always just enough and no more. The descriptions are elegant and to the point. It focuses well on the characters introduced; everyone has an often surprising part to play in the greater novel. Theo's crisis of conscience throughout the book drew me more than the plot, as he questions who he is and who he thought he was, and he never finds an easy answer. His guilt over nearly murdering a man leads to the greater question of whether any murder is acceptable, whether done in anger, or in war, or for justice.<br /><br />There were two things I didn't like much about the book. First, the description of Mickle on the back cover hints much more strongly than the book itself that her past is relevant to the current story. She is presented as a street girl of unusual talent with a tendency to nightmare. Second, most of the twists in the plot were easy to spot. The moment Theo proposes The Oracle Priestess, it's almost certain this act is going to end up in front of the king, in one form or another, and around then it was also easy to see how Mickle would end up. This left most of the book merely to work out how it was going to get there.<br /><br />On the whole this was a good read, mostly for the moral conflict and refreshingly clean prose. The resolution strongly indicates trouble will follow Theo's choices, and I look forward to reading the sequel. I rate this book Recommended.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4284035267772618308">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/21257579-corinne" class="user" title="Corinne">Corinne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/21257579-corinne?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21257579-corinne?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21257579-corinne?shelf=adventure" class="actionLinkLite">adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21257579-corinne?shelf=action-and-battles" class="actionLinkLite">action-and-battles</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21257579-corinne?shelf=tween-reads" class="actionLinkLite">tween-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21257579-corinne?shelf=children-s-literature" class="actionLinkLite">children-s-literature</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21257579-corinne?shelf=set-in-past" class="actionLinkLite">set-in-past</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21257579-corinne?shelf=princess-culture" class="actionLinkLite">princess-culture</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1236989996">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14878787220540209449">This book has so much going for it; instead of just the good vs. evil element, we have two sets of good guys who disagree on how to fix the kingdom, and all the tension thereof. There's also a seldom found recurring theme of human failing; Theo wants to be just, but isn't sure how to do that, or how to reconcile his own sins with his disdain for other people's. What appealed to me when I read it as a child was the cast of characters, and I still really enjoy Mickle and Theo and their friends. <br /><br />Th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14878787220540209449">This book has so much going for it; instead of just the good vs. evil element, we have two sets of good guys who disagree on how to fix the kingdom, and all the tension thereof. There's also a seldom found recurring theme of human failing; Theo wants to be just, but isn't sure how to do that, or how to reconcile his own sins with his disdain for other people's. What appealed to me when I read it as a child was the cast of characters, and I still really enjoy Mickle and Theo and their friends. <br /><br />Things that just don't hold up: The Count's schemes are often so ridiculous that I don't think they would fool a child, let alone an adult. The rabid Trebezonian bit was especially terrible. I also can't believe that Carrabas would try a bunch of dopey schemes to gain the throne instead of just killing the king and queen and making it look like an accident. Nor do I believe that he wants it so badly when he already basically rules the kingdom. Nor is the king's cloud of grief a believable reason for him to be so easily tricked all the time. So, some storyline troubles for sure, but a lot of great lines and moral grey areas for kids to contemplate. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1213169221">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1213169221" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/40720690-yaasha-moriah" class="left imgcol" title="Yaasha Moriah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1425059621p2/40720690.jpg" alt="Yaasha Moriah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1213169221?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 04, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/40720690-yaasha-moriah" class="user" title="Yaasha Moriah">Yaasha Moriah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/40720690-yaasha-moriah?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40720690-yaasha-moriah?shelf=magicless-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">magicless-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1213169221">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16860625032672809838">Theo is a printer’s devil. At least, he was, until the printing of an unauthorized pamphlet attracted the attention of the law of Westmark. Now a fugitive, Theo finds unlikely companions in Las Bombas, a quack doctor; Musket, a short-tempered dwarf; and Mickle, a skinny orphan girl who swaggers by day and weeps by night.<br /><br />While Theo adjusts to life on the run, Westmark teeters on the brink of ruin. King Augustine, crippled with grief at the loss of his daughter, has left the reign of the kingdom t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16860625032672809838">Theo is a printer’s devil. At least, he was, until the printing of an unauthorized pamphlet attracted the attention of the law of Westmark. Now a fugitive, Theo finds unlikely companions in Las Bombas, a quack doctor; Musket, a short-tempered dwarf; and Mickle, a skinny orphan girl who swaggers by day and weeps by night.<br /><br />While Theo adjusts to life on the run, Westmark teeters on the brink of ruin. King Augustine, crippled with grief at the loss of his daughter, has left the reign of the kingdom to Chief Minister Cabbaras, whose tightening grip on the nation has sparked the seeds of rebellion.<br /><br />The rebel leader, Florian, is a puzzle to Theo. Why does Theo hesitate to endorse Florian’s politics, yet desperately crave Florian’s approval? Should Theo uphold the monarchy or follow Florian? Could Theo make either choice—and still keep his honor?<br /><br /><strong>Some Thoughts</strong><br />Initially, Theo believes in human goodness, but as he encounters the contradictions of human nature, he begins to doubt. The man who generously saved and sheltered an orphan child, yet who made his living by deceiving people with illusions and false promises—was he a saint or a scoundrel?<br /><br /><blockquote>“Rascal he is,” [said Musket,] “But he’s a good-natured one. Take your nobles who flog their servants, gouge their tenants, or the judges who send some wretch to be hanged—they’re honest as the day is long. Any scoundrel can be honest.” <br /><br />“But all the rest of it,” said Theo. “The Salamanca Lancers! Great Copta! Trebizonia—I wonder if he even knows where it is. Why does he put out such nonsense?” <br /><br />“No business of mine,” said Musket. “For all I know, he can’t stomach the world as he finds it. Can you?” <br /><br />Theo did not answer. He turned back to rubbing down Friska. He had been more comfortable when he had been able to judge Las Bombas a complete rogue.</blockquote><br /><br />The man who believed all men were brothers, but who was willing to kill to create such a world—was he a hypocrite or a hero? And Theo: Was he truly as good as he once thought himself?<br /><br /><blockquote>“You held back,” said Florian. “I saw you. Beware, youngster. Next time, don’t hesitate. It may cost your life.” <br /><br />“But you,” said Theo. “You didn’t hesitate. You shot him without having to think.” <br /><br />“Some things are best not thought about.” <br /><br />“I have to,” said Theo. “I have to understand... I swore then I’d never try to take another man’s life. Killing is wrong. I believed that. I still do. But now I wonder. Do I believe it because I want to be a decent man? Or—because I’m a coward?”</blockquote><br /><br />I highly recommend Westmark, not only because it is an entertaining read, but also because it raises questions that are worth asking, even if they are never fully answer.<br /><br /><em>Note: One of the quack performances involves a fake séance in which the spirits of the dead are “called up.” There is also some brief profanity.</em></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_819488107">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/819488107" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7402485-lee-penney" class="left imgcol" title="Lee Penney"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Lee Penney" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/819488107?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7402485-lee-penney" class="user" title="Lee Penney">Lee Penney</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer819488107">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2596353367442354587">I don’t remember where I picked up the recommendation for this book. It’s certainly not a recent release, originally released in 1982. It’s short and from a writer who was better known for his children’s work.<br /><br />The length was part of the appeal, I was hoping to hit two books a month in 2013 (one written, one audio), but failed. I figured I could burn through this one to kick off 2014.<br /><br />And I did get through it reasonably fast, in no small part due to the fact that I enjoyed the characters and the st</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2596353367442354587">I don’t remember where I picked up the recommendation for this book. It’s certainly not a recent release, originally released in 1982. It’s short and from a writer who was better known for his children’s work.<br /><br />The length was part of the appeal, I was hoping to hit two books a month in 2013 (one written, one audio), but failed. I figured I could burn through this one to kick off 2014.<br /><br />And I did get through it reasonably fast, in no small part due to the fact that I enjoyed the characters and the story. The cover reminded me of the old copies of Treasure Island, and it seems to take place in a similar era, without any pirates or ships though. It has a similar ruthlessness to the story, which pulls no punches, with death and murder, foul play and scoundrels aplenty.<br /><br />I had a couple of small criticisms; one being that some of the plot developments are telegraphed, making them fairly easy to spot. I’d also say, as with a lot of books, the end is over and done very quickly.<br /><br />Having said that, it was an enjoyable read, with some interesting characters, and it certainly didn’t drag. It’s part of a trilogy, and I’ll be looking for the next part (assuming I can find a copy, these need to be made into digital copies for more people to enjoy).</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2596353367442354587">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/429838899?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 28, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/682334-piggie" class="user" title="Piggie">Piggie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer429838899">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer33787081415900919">This is a book that I first read when I was young. My introduction to Lloyd Alexander was actually through the movie the Black Cauldron. And the first book I read by him was the Remarkable Journey of Prince Jenn. Llyod Alexander has a beautiful written voice. It is smooth and fluid. Very easy to read quickly, but one that is better to savor slowly. He paints pictures clearly in my mind and I never feel as though the story is paused with these paintings. This book is one of my favorites from this</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText33787081415900919">This is a book that I first read when I was young. My introduction to Lloyd Alexander was actually through the movie the Black Cauldron. And the first book I read by him was the Remarkable Journey of Prince Jenn. Llyod Alexander has a beautiful written voice. It is smooth and fluid. Very easy to read quickly, but one that is better to savor slowly. He paints pictures clearly in my mind and I never feel as though the story is paused with these paintings. This book is one of my favorites from this author. It is the story of several people coming together in a way that changes the out come of history. It talks about where the line between right and wrong lies. It asks the hard question of whether or not there are different answers. It is also a story about love without being a romance novel, which I think makes for a better way to look at the nature of loving. Loyalty is also touched upon. I think that Llyod Alexander talks about these things in a subtle way that doesn't distract the reader from the story that is being told. A complex setting, real characters and an interesting book. One that I know I will read again.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="33787081415900919">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_975334385">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/975334385" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/32478683-kaye" class="left imgcol" title="Kaye"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1403489023p2/32478683.jpg" alt="Kaye" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/975334385?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 25, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/32478683-kaye" class="user" title="Kaye">Kaye</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer975334385">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16299862665905950605">I have always loved Lloyd Alexander’s Chronicles of Prydain series, so I was eager to read this trilogy and return to his beloved style of writing. Here there is both freshness and familiarity for Alexander fans, and a great read into the bargain!<br /><br />Familiarity? I feel it largely comes from the characters of Westmark, who bear striking resemblance to the characters that inhabit Prydain. The flamboyant and exaggerating Fflewddur Fflam from the Chronicles of Prydain could almost double as Count Las B</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16299862665905950605">I have always loved Lloyd Alexander’s Chronicles of Prydain series, so I was eager to read this trilogy and return to his beloved style of writing. Here there is both freshness and familiarity for Alexander fans, and a great read into the bargain!<br /><br />Familiarity? I feel it largely comes from the characters of Westmark, who bear striking resemblance to the characters that inhabit Prydain. The flamboyant and exaggerating Fflewddur Fflam from the Chronicles of Prydain could almost double as Count Las Bombas in this book, and Taran wouldn’t miss a beat in the role of Theo. Mickle is Eilonwy, minus the latter’s feisty sarcasm and her prominence in the story. The gallant Florian reminds me of Gwydion (but I have a sneaking suspicion that he will meet a tragic fate later on in the trilogy…) Lloyd Alexander certainly has a favorite cast of characters who – though their names might switch between books – remain at heart endearing and recognizable. <br /><br />Freshness? Alexander’s writing is always fresh and fluid. His protagonists are thoughtful, and questions are raised that have no easy answer. Since the Westmark trilogy is aimed at a slightly older audience than the Prydain Chronicles, these issues are dealt with even more deeply. In a world of injustice, harsh realities, and survival, what does it mean to have honor, live truthfully, and have courage? <br /><br />Honest and affirming, fresh and familiar, I am certainly looking forward to continuing Lloyd Alexander’s Westmark trilogy.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16299862665905950605">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8864767061978841173">Oooh, this book was good. <br /><br />The story begins with Theo, who' so printer's "devil", someone who helps with the various tasks and jobs that the printer needs assistance with. Then gets a job from a suspiciously upbeat dwarf named Musket, to print a lot of copies of a pamphlet that appears to be most suspicious. They accepts, though - the profit was great, after all - but when the job begins, things take a turn for the worse, because unknowingly they're printing treasonous material. <br /><br />Things happens, A</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8864767061978841173">Oooh, this book was good. <br /><br />The story begins with Theo, who' so printer's "devil", someone who helps with the various tasks and jobs that the printer needs assistance with. Then gets a job from a suspiciously upbeat dwarf named Musket, to print a lot of copies of a pamphlet that appears to be most suspicious. They accepts, though - the profit was great, after all - but when the job begins, things take a turn for the worse, because unknowingly they're printing treasonous material. <br /><br />Things happens, Anton dies, and Theo runs away. And so the story begins.<br /><br />I liked the book. The prose was excellent! I loved the way the author wrote! The quotes are simply awesome. <br /><br />Also, Theo possesses a conscience. For a teen sucked into a world where murder and war are synonymous and are said to be for the better good, and where he's forced to go along with a scam artist because it's the only way to be safe, Theo is surprisingly guilty about it all. He questions the righteousness of every wrong thing he does, something very rare in books these days. <br /><br />It's a good read. Nothing amazing, and the characters keep their distance from the reader, but the book is a good time passer. I like it. <br /><br />And on to the sequel!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6665493260198582024">Short Review: Westmark by Lloyd Alexander - I am re-reading this 1980s series from my youth. It is not nearly as well known as Alexander's other young adult series that starts with The Book of Three and end with the High King. This series is set in a fictional 18th century european country. The King has become despondent and gone a little nuts since his only child (Augusta) disappeared 8 years ago. One of his advisors has weaseled his way into power and is trying to become the next king. But The</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6665493260198582024">Short Review: Westmark by Lloyd Alexander - I am re-reading this 1980s series from my youth. It is not nearly as well known as Alexander's other young adult series that starts with The Book of Three and end with the High King. This series is set in a fictional 18th century european country. The King has become despondent and gone a little nuts since his only child (Augusta) disappeared 8 years ago. One of his advisors has weaseled his way into power and is trying to become the next king. But Theo, a young apprentice printer is just trying to do his job. When soldiers destroy the print shop and Theo gets blamed for shooting one of the soldiers in the malay, he goes on the run. He meets up first with a con artist and a girl that teaches him that all is not well with the world and later he falls in with revolutionaries. <br /><br />This book is little more than a basic set up for the rest of the trilogy but it has a good basic story line and is a good book for 12-14 year olds.<br /><br />My full review is <a rel="nofollow" href="http://bookwi.se/westmark/" target="_blank">http://bookwi.se/westmark/</a></span>

      <a href="/user/show/2366630-evelyn" class="user" title="Evelyn">Evelyn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer57796031">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13874386528952102797">"Theo, by occupation, was a devil."<br /><br />But not for long. Soon, the well-meaning young man finds himself wanted for attempted murder and travelling with a fraudulent "magician" and his dwarf coachman. An unfortunate but talented girl called Mickle joins the trio, but the moneymaking schemes she is used in break Theo and plunge him into the second half of the stoyr. <br /><br />Meanwhile, Chief Minister Cabbarus plots to win himself the throne from the grief-stricken king, who cannot seem to forget his long-dead</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13874386528952102797">"Theo, by occupation, was a devil."<br /><br />But not for long. Soon, the well-meaning young man finds himself wanted for attempted murder and travelling with a fraudulent "magician" and his dwarf coachman. An unfortunate but talented girl called Mickle joins the trio, but the moneymaking schemes she is used in break Theo and plunge him into the second half of the stoyr. <br /><br />Meanwhile, Chief Minister Cabbarus plots to win himself the throne from the grief-stricken king, who cannot seem to forget his long-dead daughter, Princess Augusta. This Cabbarus exploits in order to remove the honest and good-hearted Doctor Torrens.<br /><br />In Nierkeeping a concentrated jailbreak arms a band of charismatic rebels and sweeps the story up to the thrilling climax.<br /><br />All of the characters are memorable. Theo "loved virtue [and:] despised injustice," feeling remorse for all of his actions and having a perhaps <em>too</em> defined conscience. He is sickened by immorality whether it belongs to friend or foe. Our antagonist, Cabbarus, is an intriguing character as well. He is a villain but I kept wanting there to be hope for him because, no matter how twisted he is, he does want the country to be great and guided by his own misguided vision.<br /><br /><a title="Westmark (Firebird) by Lloyd Alexander" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24783.Westmark__Firebird_">Westmark</a> is an exhilarating story able to lend a touch of the fantastic to a realistic country...a country torn by injustice, where no one is certain about what is right or wrong, and where power is coveted by all.<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_409505627">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/409505627" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6747285-hazel-west" class="left imgcol" title="Hazel West"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1342926415p2/6747285.jpg" alt="Hazel West" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/409505627?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 22, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6747285-hazel-west" class="user" title="Hazel West">Hazel West</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6747285-hazel-west?shelf=great-summer-reads" class="actionLinkLite">great-summer-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer409505627">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14348875202596624657">Thoughts on the Overall Book: I enjoyed this book quite a bit. I'm a huge fan of classic adventure stories and also fantasy that is more alternate universe, especially ones set during the 1700s or thereabouts like this one was. I actually have never read any of Lloyd Alexander's books before which I find rather odd now since I totally would have loved these when I was younger, but now I am definitely a fan.<br /><br />Cover--Yea or Nay: I don't hate it, but I don't like the character representations either.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14348875202596624657">Thoughts on the Overall Book: I enjoyed this book quite a bit. I'm a huge fan of classic adventure stories and also fantasy that is more alternate universe, especially ones set during the 1700s or thereabouts like this one was. I actually have never read any of Lloyd Alexander's books before which I find rather odd now since I totally would have loved these when I was younger, but now I am definitely a fan.<br /><br />Cover--Yea or Nay: I don't hate it, but I don't like the character representations either. You can tell it's a fantasy/adventure novel, but I don't like how Theo or Mickle are drawn.<br /><br />Characters: This book had the great kind of cast that one should expect in an adventure novel. Theo is a great hero; I liked the fact that he had morals and he was easily likable from the moment you meet him. Likewise so were Mucket, Las Bombas and Mickle who was an awesome female character and actually reminded me of the kind of heroines I like to write about. There were also really good supporting characters. I liked Florian and Dr. Torrens a lot. Cabbarus could have been worse but he wasn't bad for the kind of book this is either. I do prefer a more nasty villain though.<br /><br />Writing Style: Fast paced, yet not so much that there is no story line, just enough to move the story alone properly as it should be. Lloyd Alexander has a wonderful writing style. It's very classic, witty, and this book actually reminded me quite a bit of "Prisoner of Zenda", it definitely had the same feel to it.<br /><br />Problems/What bothered me: Nothing bothered me in this book, at least nothing so major I would complain about it.<br /><br />Conclusion: 4 stars, I really enjoyed this book, and I look forward to reading the rest of the trilogy and other books by the author. <br /><br />Recommended Audience: Fans of classic adventure stories will love this. People who liked "Prisoner of Zenda" and books like that should definitely try this one out. It's suitable for any age.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14348875202596624657">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/5644636-andrea" class="user" title="Andrea">Andrea</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer181591591">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6267405722722920448">This book was a little hard to get into at first, but it quickly rounded out. May I say, Lloyd Alexander is an absolute prodigy. He is so far the only author that can twist a story so much that I never can figure out what's going to happen! This is a rare and dangerous feat...not to be snorted at! :P<br /><br />I love how this world is so realistic, yet so different...(then again, it's an oppressing ruler who is slowly but surely bringing about the demise of teh country...is this familiar??) And the charact</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6267405722722920448">This book was a little hard to get into at first, but it quickly rounded out. May I say, Lloyd Alexander is an absolute prodigy. He is so far the only author that can twist a story so much that I never can figure out what's going to happen! This is a rare and dangerous feat...not to be snorted at! :P<br /><br />I love how this world is so realistic, yet so different...(then again, it's an oppressing ruler who is slowly but surely bringing about the demise of teh country...is this familiar??) And the characters! Mr. Alexander has quite a talent for making great characters. Mickle was so very complex, and so entertaining! Theo--such an innocent-but-really-not soul, I could almost HEAR every thought running through his brain! And Las Bombas...sometimes I wanted to slap him silly, while other times I could only crow in laughter! As for Musket, Demon Coachman indeed! :) And Cabbarus...Mr. Alexander has an uncanny knack of creating good characters, but his villains are by far the best. Well, I like the heroines, too...OH I CAN'T DECIDE!!!! (Which is a rather enjoyable predicament to have, wouldn't you agree?) <br /><br />The plot, while a little slow at first, was intriguing! After letting the book sit for a while, I picked it up (I was about a quarter of the way through) and finished it in an afternoon! Don't you think that finishing a book in a day is so ever satisfying??<br /><br />I would recommend this book to everyone, although it wasn't one of my FAVORITE favorites! </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_128169386">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128169386" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/848564-marty" class="left imgcol" title="Marty"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1202315158p2/848564.jpg" alt="Marty" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/128169386?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 02, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/848564-marty" class="user" title="Marty">Marty</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/848564-marty?shelf=front-room-bookshelf" class="actionLinkLite">front-room-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/848564-marty?shelf=acquired" class="actionLinkLite">acquired</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/848564-marty?shelf=to-read-with-the-kids" class="actionLinkLite">to-read-with-the-kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer128169386">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18084892023218836270">As a youth, someone directed me to Lloyd Alexander, and after my first experience with him, I had no choice but to clear out the library's--what I felt to be--meager offering of Alexander material. Westmark and its following two books were one of the most memorable part of that shelf. Recently, I hoped to revisit his works and finally the opportunity presented itself. As an adult, I am still in awe at Alexander's skills as a writer.<br /><br />But first things first. The book that I have proudly blazons Llo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18084892023218836270">As a youth, someone directed me to Lloyd Alexander, and after my first experience with him, I had no choice but to clear out the library's--what I felt to be--meager offering of Alexander material. Westmark and its following two books were one of the most memorable part of that shelf. Recently, I hoped to revisit his works and finally the opportunity presented itself. As an adult, I am still in awe at Alexander's skills as a writer.<br /><br />But first things first. The book that I have proudly blazons Lloyd Alexander as the "Grand Master of Fantasy"! I'm not sure exactly what that means, besides that it sounds cultish ("grand master"?!) and does more for inspiring me to avoid the book than for picking it up. But I do feel impelled to point out that this book is fantasy in only a very loose definition of the word. The nation that Alexander has created does not exist in the real world, granted, (I would call that fictional, more than fantasy), but there is no "magic" or other-worldly creatures. It is more like an alternate history. Or, if my instincts serve me correctly, the events of the French revolution occurring within the same geographic space as the country of Wales (Alexander had a thing for Wales, which was a basis for his actual "fantasy" series, the Prydain Chronicles). So, if you are turned off by fantasy, don't let the premise that this is a fantasy novel keep you from enjoying what is really best described as a fictional piece.<br /><br />As for the writing, it is awe-inspiring. Well, to me. To anyone else, it would just seem pretty simple and straight forward. To me, it is awe inspiring that Lloyd Alexander can take a setting, situation, and characters that the greats like Hugo and Dickens played around with, and he can portray the same ideas in infinitely abridged form. Probably a lot of the reason for this is due to work those two greats did in establishing such a vivid world which can easily be drawn upon ... however, it is a tribute to Alexander that he can so effortlessly dip into their worlds and bring out something completely original and still quite powerful. Also amazing to me is that for a world that is so packed with personality, Alexander does not seem to pause for exposition, at all. And yet we don't feel left in the dark, in fact, we feel enriched by the world that the characters inhabit. At the same time, the characters are full characters, with their own life--not just empty forms filling a set plot purpose. True, the characters don't reach nearly the depth that Dickens or Hugo can attain, even with their side characters. Yet it is admirable that these characters are still complex considering the limits of length and audience that Alexander is dealing with. Also impressive is that each chapter has quite a bit of action and leaves you pressing for more. The plot rides along smoothly, with an interesting gem coming every couple of pages, not a chapter extraneous or boring. All of these things amaze me. Being a young adult writer, I am more and more understanding, requires a skill set equal to if not greater than many other adult fiction writers--and Lloyd Alexander has to be considered as one of the perfect examples of how to do that correctly.<br /><br />Anyway, as I am reading the whole trilogy, which is really like one, single novel, you will be hearing more from me on Lloyd Alexander, but I'll try to focus more on the story for the next two books than I have here. Still, it is a wonderful experience to read his books--one that does not require a lot of investment, and something that your kids will enjoy. If you're like me, you'll just have to enjoy it on your own until your kids are old enough to do so with you.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18084892023218836270">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
